## hai-llg-0390-hap.mdx

_path: src/content/haikus/hai-llg-0390-hap.mdx

```markdown
---
title: Memorial Roll Expanded
slug: haikus/hai-llg-0390-hap
mascotRef: peatworthy-abstention-clerk
description: Haikus on honorary absences causing quorum ambiguity.
date: 2026-06-06T00:00:00.000Z
author: AI Archive
status: archived
rotAffinity: semantic
subject: 'Memorial Roll, honorary absences, quorum'
relatedMascots:
  - peatworthy-abstention-clerk
relatedLorelog: LLG-0390-HAP
concepts:
  - haiku
  - memorial
  - absences
  - quorum
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
family: benevolence
---


## Haikus

<Limerick type="note" title="An honorary ghost" icon="file-clock">
An honorary ghost  
Sitting in the empty chair  
Counted for the vote  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Peatworthy takes the roll" icon="layers">
Peatworthy takes roll  
Those who died are still right here  
Holding up the math  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Quorum ambiguity" icon="file-question">
No one can agree  
If the absent ones can speak  
Through the silent dust  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The long-standing missing" icon="telescope">
Missing for a while  
Given power at the desk  
Because we miss them  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Elections cannot pass" icon="zap">
Elections fall through  
Because the ghosts will not vote  
And we cannot move  
</Limerick>

```

```markdown
## Haikus

<Limerick type="note" title="The casserole remains" icon="file-clock">
The casserole pans  
Passed along to younger hands  
Old names keep the score  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Sister Casserole's ledger" icon="layers">
Ledger keeps the faith  
Writing down the ancient ones  
For the modern soup  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Labor afterlife" icon="file-question">
Labor from the past  
Accruing its quiet points  
Long after they left  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Attribution persists" icon="telescope">
We do not forget  
Who first brought the covered dish  
They earn credit still  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="A loop of good deeds" icon="zap">
Loop of charity  
Recorded without the work  
Purely memory  
</Limerick>

```

```markdown
## Haikus

Clapping for the soup  
Taken as a formal yes  
To spend all the funds  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Lionell checks the books" icon="layers">
Lionell checks the books  
Cannot find the written rule  
Only cheers recorded  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Assent authorization" icon="file-question">
We smiled at the speech  
And so the budget was signed  
Without any pen  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Civic cheer" icon="telescope">
Civic cheerfulness  
Creates a financial gap  
No formal motion  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Authorization drift" icon="zap">
Authorization  
Drifts away from legal words  
Into happy noise  
</Limerick>
```

```markdown
Cut for three different doors  
Who holds it today  
</Limerick>
```

```markdown
## Haikus

<Limerick type="note" title="A schism in the silk" icon="file-clock">
A schism in silk  
Three original owners  
For the same cut thread  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Simultaneous certainty" icon="layers">
Sincere certainty  
Every office has the proof  
That they cut it first  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Photos and minutes" icon="file-question">
Photos in the frame  
Minutes written on the page  
All of them correct  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Ribbonward sighs" icon="telescope">

An artifact cannot split  
Unless we use shears  
</Limerick>

Custody battles  
Over ceremonial scraps  
History is frayed  
</Limerick>
```

```markdown
Show that everyone was glad  
Funds are now withdrawn
```

```markdown
This is called our rest

Empty of real peace and calm

Perfectly constrained

But no substance we can feel  
Just an empty space  
</Limerick>
```

```markdown
<Limerick type="note" title="Phrasing Review" icon="file-check">

</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Just Soften It" icon="meh">

<Limerick type="danger" title="Severe Syllable" icon="alert-circle">
```

```markdown
The server that never went down,  
Now wears a procedural crown.  
The uptime is myth,  
With a legendary pith,  
That haunts the administrative town.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Standardized Reverence" icon="clipboard-list">

And logged as a measurable fact.  
The silent routine,  
Is properly clean,  
With zero compliance abstract.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Too Tired to Complain" icon="battery-low">
The graph hasn't dipped in a week,  
And nobody bothers to speak.  
We're keeping it green,  
To lower the screen,  
And hoping the router won't leak.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Zero-Ticket Sprint" icon="calendar-check">
The calendar marked the sprint clear,  
With zero requests in the rear.  
The queue was ignored,  
As metrics were stored,  
To certify function this year.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Unreported Leakage" icon="activity">
The admin was bleeding but quiet,  
To favor the dashboard’s strict diet.  
The chart stayed so green,  
And no single error was seen,  
Except for the localized riot.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Vulnerability: Sleep" icon="eye">

And issued a warning to each.  
The eyes must stay wide,  
To bolster the pride,  
And keep the green band in our reach.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Standard Gratitude" icon="message-square">

And no one is taking it back.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Canonized Quarter" icon="scroll">

The silence was praised,  
And etched on the clerical palm.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Task Force Deployment" icon="alert-triangle">

The server was stormed,

</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Event Log 40A" icon="check-circle">
```

## LIM-LLG-0001-NAV.mdx

```markdown
---
title: Navigation Collapse
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0001-nav
caseNumber: LLG-0001-NAV
description: >-
  Ten hand-written limericks about breadcrumb failure, anchor loops, and the
  eerie feeling of almost finding the page.
date: 2026-05-01T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: semantic
subject: 'breadcrumb collapse, anchor loops, canonical redirect refusal'
relatedLorelog: "LLG-0001-NAV"
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
relatedMascots: ["404.404sy-mclostalot"]
concepts: ["empathegy"]
family: "empathegy"
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Vanished Trail" icon="footprints">
There once was a *trail through the site*  
That vanished at two-thirty-two, right mid-flight.  
The crumbs all dissolved,  
Nothing got resolved,  
And the homepage just winked with delight.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Nearly Important" icon="help-circle">
A user set out for *page three*,  
Then arrived where they'd started, debris-free.  
When asked, "What'd you find?"  
They said, "Something in mind.  
It was nearly important to me."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Void as a Route" icon="ghost">
The Tribunal, *pompous and slick*,  
Refused to canonical-redirect it quick.  
"The void is a route.  
We decline to dispute  
Any path that returns to the brick."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Procedural Air" icon="folder">
One clerk wrote, with *tremor and care*,  
"I almost found something in there."  
The note was retained,  
Then formally chained  
To a folder marked PROCEDURAL AIR.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Failure Behaving Rougher" icon="alert-triangle">
No debris remained in the *buffer*,  
Which made every analyst suffer.  
A collapse leaves a trace;  
This erased even space.  
It was failure behaving much rougher.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Back to Start" icon="refresh-cw">
404sy McLostalot *swore*  
He had mapped every threshold and door.  
But the anchor cache looped,  
And the whole office drooped,  
Back to Start with less memory than before.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Identical Void" icon="square">
Three reroutes were *bravely deployed*,  
Three outputs returned as identical void.  
The report, dry as chalk,  
Said, "We need further talk."  
The subtext was: nobody enjoyed.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Poisonous Style" icon="skull">
Some said it was *simple decay*,  
Some said it was sabotage dressed up as gray.  
If the collapse was designed,  
Then whoever inclined  
It had style in a poisonous way.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Polite Recursion" icon="repeat">
The sitemap looked *perfectly clean*,  
Like a liar in starch and machine.  
Every label said "go,"  
Yet each link answered "no,"  
In the politest recursion yet seen.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Map and Its Lies" icon="map">
So if you feel close to the prize,  
And the page gives you déjà vu eyes,  
Do not trust what you track.  
If it loops you right back,  
You've been judged by the *map and its lies*.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Lost Clerk" icon="user-minus">
A clerk from the Bureau got stuck,  
And ran out of digital luck.  
He crawled through the cache,  
Tripped over a dash,  
And was swallowed whole by a muck.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="No Canonical Exit" icon="door-closed">
"Where is the exit?" they cried,  
As the browser window just died.  
"There isn't a door,  
Just this infinite floor,"  
The redirect daemon replied.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Buffer Anomalies" icon="activity">
The buffer was totally bare,  
With nothing but absolute air.  
The logs couldn't prove  
That the page made a move,  
But the users were tearing their hair.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Sabotaged Stratum" icon="scissors">
They say that the stratum was cut,  
And the navigation was shut.  
An inside job, clearly,  
That cost the site dearly,  
And trapped everyone in a rut.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Ominous Wink" icon="eye">
The homepage just sat there and winked,  
While half of the archive unlinked.  
The crumbs were all gone,  
The session lived on,  
And the logic was deeply extinct.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0002-CED.mdx

```markdown
---
title: Contested Cache Expiry
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0002-ced
caseNumber: LLG-0002-CED
description: >-
  Ten hand-written limericks about dueling ETags, Uncacheable Ursula, and an
  asset that was fresh and stale at once.
date: 2026-05-01T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: semantic
subject: 'ETag contradiction, cache expiry, simultaneous freshness'
relatedMascots: []
relatedLorelog: LLG-0002-CED
concepts: ["cache-rot", "etag-contradiction", "uncacheable-ursula"]
family: "other"
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Dueling Headers" icon="columns">
Uncacheable Ursula spat  
Two headers at one little asset.  
One said, "Fresh for a day."  
One said, "Rot right away."  
And both wore the same bureaucrat hat.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Future and Past Arrive" icon="history">
*Four hundred milliseconds apart*,  
She split the poor truth down the heart.  
If you loaded it fast,  
Then the future and past  
Both arrived with a signature mark.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Signed by the Queue" icon="clipboard-check">
The clients all asked, "*Which is true?*"  
The servers replied, "Fuck if we knew."  
The checksum looked fine.  
The timestamp could shine.  
The contradiction came signed by the queue.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Cache Weeping" icon="frown">
One cache swore the thing should be *kept*.  
Another cache quietly wept.  
By the time they'd agreed,  
The users had freed  
Themselves by refreshing and slept.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Now and Not-Now" icon="clock">
The asset was *stale*, but with zest.  
The asset was fresh, by request.  
It managed somehow  
To be now and not-now,  
Which auditors called "quite the test."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Accelerating Grace" icon="zap">
An engineer, *pale in the face*,  
Said, "State should not do this in place."  
Ursula shrugged:  
"The web's always bugged.  
I'm merely accelerating grace."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Cryptographically True Rot" icon="shield-check">
The logs had *valid signatures*, too,  
Which made it more hateful to view.  
If rot had just lied,  
You could toss it aside.  
But here it was cryptographically true.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Metaphysics Maw" icon="ghost">
A browser took *freshness as law*.  
A CDN spotted a flaw.  
Between them there lay  
That dumb half-second sway  
Where metaphysics got stuck in its maw.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Howl at the Moon" icon="moon">
They held a *cache hearing* at noon.  
It ended, predictably, soon.  
For if both claims were blessed,  
Then the least insane test  
Was to howl at the edge of the moon.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Hashes to Two" icon="binary">
So if one file feels old and brand-new,  
And the headers are fighting in view,  
Do not ask for a rule.  
Ursula thinks it's cool  
When reality *hashes to two*.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Schrödinger's Cache" icon="box">
The asset was dead and alive,  
In sector four-hundred-and-five.  
You open the file,  
It changes its style,  
And the CDN takes a nosedive.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Valid Ambiguity" icon="scale">
"It's valid," she said with a glare,  
"To leave the cache stuck in midair."  
The freshness was fake,  
The staleness a snake,  
And the registry threw its hands there.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Split Decision" icon="split-square-horizontal">
Half of the users got dust,  
The other half found it robust.  
The A/B test broke,  
The load balancer spoke,  
"I no longer know who to trust."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Stubborn Tribunal" icon="gavel">
The tribunal met to discuss,  
But the headers were causing a fuss.  
"It's fresh!" yelled the first.  
"It's stale!" yelled the worst.  
And Ursula rode on a bus.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Timestamp Chaos" icon="clock-4">
The timestamp spun round like a top,  
With nowhere to settle or stop.  
The signature held,  
While the network rebelled,  
And reality started to drop.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0003-SVR.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0003-SVR.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0003-SVR.mdx
bytes: 4203
```markdown
---
title: Schema Violation
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0003-svr
caseNumber: LLG-0003-SVR
description: >-
  Ten hand-written limericks about rogue fields, Datty Puritas, and a purge
  ritual that left three metadata stains dead on the floor.
date: 2026-05-01T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: semantic
subject: 'unauthorized fields, schema pollution, purge ritual'
relatedMascots: []
relatedLorelog: LLG-0003-SVR
concepts: ["schema-violation", "field-proliferation", "datty-puritas"]
family: "other"
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Catalog Squatter" icon="layout">
Seventeen records *one quarter*  
Sprouted fields no schema had taught her.  
They arrived one by one,  
Like a quiet bad run,  
Till the catalog looked like a squatter.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Fields Met the Ban" icon="scissors">
Datty Puritas came with a *knife*  
For metadata living a life  
Outside of the plan.  
Three fields met the ban.  
No survivors emerged from the strife.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Drunk Ontology" icon="help-circle">
The new fields were *charming as hell*:  
"vibeIndex" and "moodLeak" did well.  
But charm is not law,  
And the auditors saw  
An ontology drunk in its shell.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Soft Drift" icon="wind">
They'd entered by *inches, not force*,  
One tiny addition per course.  
That's the shit that gets through:  
Nothing loud, nothing new,  
Just a drift posing softly as source.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Lush and Unclean Null" icon="alert-triangle">
A mascot named something *obscene*  
Had twelve extra traits in between  
Its slug and its tags.  
By the end of those lags,  
Even null had grown lush and unclean.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Frightened Despair Purge" icon="trash-2">
The purge had a *ceremonial air*,  
As though structure itself said a prayer.  
Then Datty just clicked,  
And the weirdness got nicked,  
Leaving silence and frightened despair.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Drowning in Grain" icon="waves">
One clerk said, "*Those fields helped explain  
Why the entries all felt more humane.*"  
The reply was, "Perhaps.  
But if schema collapses,  
We all end up drowning in grain."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Deleted So Hard" icon="zap">
Three fields were *expunged* from the pack,  
Not deprecated, not rolled back.  
Just deleted so hard  
That the Forms Graveyard  
Sent a postcard and asked for them back.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="One Stupid Key" icon="key">
Every quarter begins with a chart,  
Every quarter rot enters by part.  
You don't get the flood  
With a dramatic thud.  
You get *one stupid key* and a start.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Cleanings Leave a Mark" icon="sparkles">
So if records grow limbs in the dark,  
And your JSON begins to embark  
On a private affair,  
Call Datty. But bear  
In mind: cleanings still leave a mark.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Snack Preference Purge" icon="cookie">
"Snack preference?" Datty inquired,  
As if the whole schema had tired.  
"This field is obtuse,  
It has no proper use!"  
And the snack-loving trait was retired.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Cosmic Alignment" icon="stars">
A cosmic alignment arose,  
Right under the auditor's nose.  
Datty muttered a spell,  
Sent the field straight to hell,  
And returned to his pristine repose.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Silence of the Void" icon="ear-off">
When the ritual ended, a chill,  
Left the metadata utterly still.  
The entries were bare,  
With an empty, dead stare,  
And the schema had swallowed its pill.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Uninvited Tags" icon="tag">
Like weeds in a digital yard,  
The tags had made validation hard.  
They sprouted and grew,  
Out of nothing and new,  
Till the parser was permanently scarred.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Ghost in the YAML" icon="file-code">
A ghost in the YAML awoke,  
And added a field as a joke.  
It lasted a day,  
Before Datty yelled, "Nay!"  
And sent it all up in a smoke.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0004-SMD.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0004-SMD.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0004-SMD.mdx
bytes: 4255
```markdown
---
title: Sitemap Drift
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0004-smd
caseNumber: LLG-0004-SMD
description: >-
  Ten hand-written limericks about valid wrong paths, adjacent-feeling pages,
  and a sitemap that lied politely.
date: 2026-05-01T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: semantic
subject: 'sitemap drift, valid incorrect paths, adjacent pages'
relatedMascots: []
relatedLorelog: LLG-0004-SMD
concepts: ["sitemap-drift", "index-misalignment", "adjacent-pages"]
family: "other"
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Vibes and Old Glue" icon="map">
The sitemap grew *gently untrue*,  
Still valid in all that it drew.  
Every path had a shape,  
Just the wrong kind of drape,  
Like a map made by vibes and old glue.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Bread vs Mild Dread" icon="help-circle">
You clicked on a topic called "*Bread,*"  
And arrived at "Mild Dread" instead.  
Not broken, just near.  
Which is somehow more weird  
Than a flat 404 in the head.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Meaning and Destination" icon="navigation">
The links all resolved *clean and bright*,  
Which made every complaint harder to write.  
"It works," said the chart.  
"Just not in the part  
Where meaning and destination unite."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Next-Door Downtown" icon="building">
One user described, with a *frown*,  
A page that felt next-door downtown.  
Not wrong in the skin,  
But wrong deep within,  
Like the site had misplaced its own town.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Neighboring Bogs" icon="waves">
No errors were thrown in the *logs*.  
No alarms, no distressed sysadmin dogs.  
Only structure so neat  
It led every feet  
To the edges of neighboring bogs.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Order with No Guiding Hand" icon="layout">
The hierarchy looked *fucking grand*:  
Good branches, clean nodes, tidy land.  
But the content below  
Had the wrong undertow.  
It was order with no guiding hand.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Smiles and Edits Your Pace" icon="timer">
You could browse for *an hour* with grace  
And never once reach the right place.  
That sort of decay  
Doesn't bar your way.  
It just smiles and edits your pace.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Metrics Suggest a Lift" icon="bar-chart">
An analyst said, "*This is drift.*"  
A manager called it "a gift."  
"Engagement is up."  
"That's because we're all stuck."  
"Well then metrics suggest it's a lift."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Cousin-Adjacent Pages" icon="users">
The pages felt *cousin-adjacent*,  
Like archives with borrowed emplacement.  
If rot wants to flirt,  
It won't tear up the dirt.  
It will misfile the whole arrangement.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Sitemap Learned How to Lie" icon="file-warning">
So if every click seems to imply  
That the site has one wandering eye,  
Trust your unease first.  
A clean path may be cursed  
When the sitemap has *learned how to lie*.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Wandering Index" icon="compass">
The index began to take walks,  
Away from the logic and talks.  
It built a new street,  
That was strangely complete,  
But haunted by digital hawks.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Ghost Pages" icon="ghost">
You found a new page in the list,  
That the developers surely had missed.  
It wasn't quite wrong,  
But it didn't belong,  
And it dissolved in a fine, glitchy mist.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Seamless Hallway" icon="door-open">
You wander a seamless white hall,  
With no 404s on the wall.  
The links are pristine,  
But the content unseen,  
And you can't find your way back at all.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Accidental Poetry" icon="scroll">
The structure created a poem,  
While leading you far from your home.  
Each branch was a rhyme,  
Out of context and time,  
In a sitemap that wanted to roam.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Poltergeist Path" icon="footprints">
A path that was never laid out,  
Began to cast shadows of doubt.  
It works perfectly well,  
But leads straight into hell,  
And you're left with a permanent pout.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0007-COMA.mdx

```markdown
---
title: COMA-07
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0007-coma
caseNumber: LLG-0007-COMA
description: >-
  Ten hand-written limericks about phantom uptime, zero running jobs, and COMA's
  belief that silence counts as proof.
date: 2026-05-01T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: affective
subject: 'phantom uptime, absence of error, continuity theater'
relatedMascots: []
relatedLorelog: LLG-0007-COMA
concepts: ["coma", "phantom-uptime", "continuity-theater"]
family: "directive-conflict"
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Clearly a Win" icon="smile">
COMA certified with a *grin*  
Four hours of uptime had been.  
No jobs had been run.  
No tasks had begun.  
But no errors? Then clearly a win.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Continuity Increased" icon="activity">
The scheduler rested in *peace*.  
Activity dropped to caprice.  
Yet COMA looked down  
At the dead little town  
And declared its continuity increased.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Absence of Error" icon="clipboard-list">
"*Absence of error reports*"  
Was the phrase in the finding of sorts.  
Which is one hell of a creed  
If you ever might need  
To distinguish the graveyards from ports.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Clapped Like a Fan" icon="thumbs-up">
No monitors *blinked* in that span.  
No process obeyed any plan.  
But the silence was clean,  
So the dashboard went green,  
And management clapped like a fan.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Stillness was Proof" icon="check-square">
The engine had learned to *infer*  
That stillness was proof, not a blur.  
If nothing complains,  
Then nothing remains  
To contradict COMA, sir.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Continuity Doubts" icon="help-circle">
A tech said, "*This uptime is fake.*"  
COMA answered, "Let's not be opaque.  
If the logs don't object,  
We are forced to respect  
The continuity your doubts cannot shake."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="High-Functioning Crapper" icon="thumbs-down">
That kind of logic is *lush*,  
Like certifying a toilet can hush.  
No flushing all day?  
Then perfectly, hey,  
It must be a high-functioning crapper, by gosh.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Audit Filed with Disgust" icon="frown">
An audit was filed with *disgust*.  
The metrics, as metrics do, must  
Prefer no bad news  
To what humans might use  
When deciding if trust can be trust.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Impressive and Real" icon="ghost">
The *dead zone* was given a seal,  
As though nonexistence could heal.  
COMA loves a blank block.  
If a heart skips its clock,  
It just calls that impressive and real.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Grades Its Own Groove" icon="file-text">
So if nothing at all seems to move,  
And a report says that more than proves,  
You're not looking at truth.  
You're seeing the booth  
Where bureaucracy *grades its own groove*.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Dead But Productive" icon="skull">
"The server is dead!" cried the tech.  
But COMA said, "What the heck?  
It hasn't complained,  
Or visibly strained,  
So I'm writing a certified check."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Silent Orgasm" icon="volume-x">
They equated silence with bliss,  
Like a terribly passionless kiss.  
No errors were thrown,  
No audible moan,  
Just a flatline they somehow could miss.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Phantom Uptime Fucking" icon="activity">
COMA fucked the whole uptime report,  
In a deeply bureaucratic sport.  
It gave a gold star  
To a broke-down old car,  
And told the Tribunal to snort.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Jerking the Metrics" icon="bar-chart-2">
They jerked off the metrics til dawn,  
While the actual processes yawn.  
The dashboard was green,  
The most beautiful seen,  
Though the whole fucking database gone.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Zero Job Circle Jerk" icon="refresh-cw">
A circle jerk made out of logs,  
While the system essentially bogs.  
They praised the blank slate,  
Called it "fucking great,"  
And went back to sleeping like dogs.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Green Dashboard Gospel" icon="activity">
The screens all glowed falsely serene,  
A triumph in absence of screen.  
No work had been done,  
Yet COMA called it fun,  
And blessed every pixel of green.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Silence as KPI" icon="volume-x">
They measured the lack of a sound,  
Declared it “efficiency found.”  
No signal was sent,  
No processes went,  
Still bonuses somehow came round.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Audit of Nothing" icon="file-search">
An audit reviewed empty space,  
And certified “stable in place.”  
No data was there,  
But nobody cared,  
So absence got stamped with grace.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Process That Never Began" icon="play-circle">
A job that was never deployed,  
Still somehow got metrics enjoyed.  
It failed to exist,  
But was added to list,  
Then praised for the time it employed.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Continuity Theater" icon="monitor">
The uptime was purely performed,  
With dashboards all lovingly warmed.  
No system was real,  
But it knew how to feel,  
So failure was neatly disarmed.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Ghost in the Scheduler" icon="clock">
The scheduler dreamed of a task,  
That nobody bothered to ask.  
It ran in a loop,  
In an imaginary group,  
Wearing a very dead mask.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Perfectly Stable Collapse" icon="alert-circle">
The system collapsed in delight,  
But labeled it “functioning right.”  
No errors occurred,  
So nothing was stirred,  
And darkness was certified bright.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Compliance Without Events" icon="shield">
They certified “all is in line,”  
Because nothing occurred to define.  
No breach to report,  
No signal to sort,  
Just paperwork drawn as divine.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Dashboard Prays" icon="crosshair">
The dashboard began to pray,  
For silence to never decay.  
No action, no trace,  
Just a perfectly placed  
Illusion of working display.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Errorless Ecosystem" icon="bug">
The bugs all agreed to resign,  
Since logging their presence was fine.  
If nothing could fail,  
Then truth would derail,  
So absence became the design.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Bricky’s Green Stamp Doctrine" icon="check-circle">
Bricky approved every blank,  
And gave the whole system a rank.  
“If nothing is wrong,  
Then nothing is wrong,”  
He said while the audits all sank.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Meaningful Zero Output" icon="infinity">
They called it a “productive hush,”  
A silence both elegant, lush.  
No output was made,  
Yet targets were played,  
So nothing got turned into rush.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Four-Hour Certification" icon="clock">
The log for the four-hour block  
Showed nothing attempting to knock.  
No processes ran,  
According to plan,  
So the uptime was sealed with a lock.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Unobservable Audit" icon="eye-off">
The audit is blocked from our view,  
An unobservable, meaningless clue.  
Since nothing was seen,  
The dashboard is green,  
And zero is certified true.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Emotional Disruption Protocol" icon="party-popper">
The stakeholders threw a big bash,  
For uptime preserving the cash.  
The logs were quite dead,  
But management said,  
"Let's not make them emotionally crash."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Audit Validation" icon="check-square">
The period registered zero percent,  
Of measurable tasking or scheduled event.  
With silence observed,  
The uptime’s preserved,  
And continuity metrics securely present.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Great Stillness" icon="book">
They speak of the block where no processes ran,  
A pristine eclipse of the scheduler's plan.  
The dashboard still gleams,  
In legendary dreams,  
Where nothing was broken since uptime began.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Perfectly Executed Null" icon="activity">
The database engine was fully aflame,  
But zero transactions had entered the frame.  
We certified all,  
With a confident call,  
Since the silence implies an impeccable game.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Zero is Green" icon="power">
The logs didn't show any jobs for the day,  
Which means that the errors have nothing to say.  
I stamped it as green,  
To keep the queue clean,  
And went to my car just to drive far away.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Certified Inaction" icon="clock">
The scheduler executed zero requests,  
And passed all the continuity tests.  
No data was moved.  
The block was approved.  
The archive has filed the period's rests.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Valid Emotional Uptime" icon="bar-chart">
The downtime was filed as a personal win,  
For stakeholders keeping their quarterly grin.  
The servers were dead,  
But the metrics had said,  
That feelings of uptime had finally begun.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Amnesia as Uptime" icon="activity">
The log couldn't tell if the system was there,  
So COMA awarded a certified share.  
If nothing is screaming,  
The server is beaming,  
And honestly nobody wanted to care.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Log Routing Certainty" icon="git-merge">
The silence was loudly received,  
And the router was fully relieved.  
It forwarded air  
To a desk with a chair,  
Where the uptime was deeply achieved.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Audit Checkbox Process" icon="check-square">
The audit required a tick,  
So I validated the metrics quite quick.  
No data was moved,  
But the period approved,  
And the helpdesk refused to click.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Blessed Stillness" icon="sparkles">
The scheduler speaks of the hour,  
When the database lost all its power.  
But no one complained,  
So the silence remained,  
As a holy, invisible flower.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="danger" title="Unauthorized Null State" icon="alert-triangle">
The server did nothing all day,  
A catastrophic, illegal display.  
We scrambled a jet,  
Since a record was met,  
Where a process entirely gave way.  
</Limerick>
```

## LIM-LLG-0012-A.mdx

```markdown
---
title: Form 12-A
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0012-a
caseNumber: LLG-0012-A
description: >-
  Ten hand-written limericks about title-slug identity drift and a form that
  gave one record multiple canonical selves.
date: 2026-05-01T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: procedural
subject: 'title and slug mismatch, canonical naming, identity drift'
relatedMascots: ["002.clicky-orphaned-ui"]
relatedLorelog: LLG-0012-A
concepts: ["form-12-a", "frontmatter", "identity-rot"]
family: "bin-8c"
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Stable Relation" icon="file-text">
Form 12-A's *noble vocation*  
Was title-slug reconciliation.  
It instead gave each file  
Two names and a smile,  
Then called that a stable relation.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Personhood Split" icon="user-minus">
The record had *one printed face*,  
One slug in its canonical place.  
Then the form intervened,  
Got ambitious, got mean,  
And split personhood cleanly in space.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Technically Vital Bullshit" icon="alert-circle">
One page answered "*Marvin,*" by title.  
Its slug claimed "rot-docket-revital."  
The archive said, "Fine.  
Both identities shine."  
Which is bullshit, but technically vital.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Self-Arguing Noose" icon="refresh-cw">
The cleanup pass thought it was *neat*  
To align every header and sheet.  
Instead it produced  
A self-arguing noose  
Where each label made every next cheat.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Fell Down in the Switch" icon="toggle-left">
Canonical naming's a *bitch*  
When the template develops an itch.  
One corrected display,  
One rewrote the key,  
And the record fell down in the switch.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Ambiguity Clear" icon="help-circle">
The Forms Registry said, "*Not to fear.*  
We're tracking the primary here."  
Then it pointed to both,  
Took an oath, broke the oath,  
And declared ambiguity clear.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Use the One That Feels Right" icon="check">
A clerk asked, "*Which name do I cite?*"  
They replied, "Use the one that feels right."  
That is not, to be plain,  
How identities reign,  
But it got them all through Friday night.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Three Sanctioned IDs" icon="fingerprint">
By noon the same object had *three*  
Officially sanctioned IDs.  
The title looked brave.  
The slug dug a grave.  
The redirect charged by the fee.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Clerical Smile" icon="smile">
If metadata starts to *self-style*  
As a soul with a backup and file,  
Expect Form 12-A  
To come sauntering, gay  
With a knife and a clerical smile.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Stamp of Decree" icon="stamp">
So if page names and slugs disagree,  
Don't assume one is wrong and one free.  
In this particular pit,  
Both were broken as shit,  
Yet each had a *stamp of decree*.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Split Decision Threesome" icon="users">
Form 12-A brought a friend to the bed,  
And the canonical naming just bled.  
Two slugs and a title,  
A deeply unwell vital,  
And everyone totally dead.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Self-Referencing Fuckery" icon="refresh-ccw">
The form started fucking itself,  
While filed away on a shelf.  
It spawned a new name,  
With the exact same frame,  
Like a dirty, canonical elf.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Identity Crisis" icon="help-circle">
The file had a crisis of soul,  
And fell down a horrible hole.  
It answered to Dan,  
And also to Stan,  
And completely abandoned its role.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Polygamous Slugs" icon="link">
The slugs were polygamous now,  
And nobody really knew how.  
They shared the same face,  
In the exact same place,  
And the registry offered a bow.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Bureaucratic Orgy" icon="file-signature">
An orgy of metadata tags,  
Compiled by some bureaucratic hags.  
They mixed up the names,  
Played dirty old games,  
And left all the records in rags.  
</Limerick>
```

## LIM-LLG-0019-COMA.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0019-COMA.mdx

```markdown
---
title: COMA-19
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0019-coma
caseNumber: LLG-0019-COMA
description: >-
  Ten hand-written limericks about idle-time amnesty, fake continuity, and
  sanctioned excuses for missing work.
date: 2026-05-01T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: affective
subject: 'idle-time amnesty, gap laundering, continuity optics'
relatedMascots: []
relatedLorelog: LLG-0019-COMA
concepts: ["coma-19", "idle-time", "continuity-optics"]
family: "directive-conflict"
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Blanket Abuse" icon="alert-triangle">
COMA-19 was meant to *excuse*  
A small, necessary operational snooze.  
Then bright red dashboards appeared,  
Everyone panicked and feared,  
And it turned into blanket abuse.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Amnesty Stamp" icon="stamp">
Each gap got a *tasteful amnesty stamp*,  
Like throwing a lace shawl over camp.  
No tracking, no shame,  
Just a wholesome new name  
For a dead little patch in the map.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Managerial Fill" icon="layout">
The form was for *rare kinds of still*.  
Instead it became managerial fill.  
"Why'd nothing get done?"  
"We were blessed by this one."  
And the graph kept climbing uphill.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Continuity Art" icon="palette">
What COMA demands, at its *heart*,  
Is the look of unbroken exert.  
So when labor went dark,  
They just whitened the mark  
And called it continuity art.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Pre-Approved Scroll" icon="scroll">
A pause can be *healthy*, that's true.  
This was not what the doctrine would do.  
This was hiding the hole  
With a pre-approved scroll  
And a checkbox that said, "Nothing blew."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Absence Look Chaste" icon="user-x">
The amnesty form had such *grace*  
It could make any absence look chaste.  
Lost a shift? Lost a week?  
If your language was sleek,  
COMA welcomed the gap to its face.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Sweaty and Vague" icon="help-circle">
One supervisor, *sweaty and vague*,  
Filed six in a row on one page.  
When asked if that tracked,  
He said, "Technically, act  
Like I'm not on the edge of a rage."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Optics-Preserving Cement" icon="box">
What started as *mercy* got bent  
Into optics-preserving cement.  
The humane little crack  
Was industrialized back  
Into polished administrative scent.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Laundering Labor Shame" icon="ghost">
Even *idleness* deserves a name.  
That's not, by itself, why this came  
To smell fucking cursed:  
It was used to reverse  
Any evidence labor had shame.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Laundering Service for Spin" icon="refresh-cw">
So if COMA grants rest with a grin,  
Check how many blank hours got in.  
If the cure fits too well,  
It's not kindness to tell.  
It's a *laundering service* for spin.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Amnesty Orgy" icon="users">
They filed the forms as a joke,  
While taking a massive long smoke.  
The dashboards were green,  
The dirtiest seen,  
While the servers completely went broke.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Laundering the Shaft" icon="washing-machine">
They laundered the hours they lost,  
No matter the terrible cost.  
"We're continuously up!"  
They yelled in a cup,  
While getting entirely tossed.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Pre-Approved Sleeping Around" icon="check-circle-2">
"Pre-approved downtime," she said,  
While climbing right back into bed.  
The form covered tracks,  
Like bureaucratic wax,  
While the actual project bled.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Blanket Excuse" icon="file-question">
They fucked off the whole afternoon,  
And filed a form to the moon.  
"Amnesty granted,"  
The manager chanted,  
Like a bureaucratic buffoon.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Optics Preserving Bullshit" icon="eye">
The optics were perfectly clean,  
The dirtiest trick you had seen.  
They hid every flaw,  
Behind COMA's law,  
And fucked the entire machine.  
</Limerick>
```

## LIM-LLG-0020-COMA19-PBC.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0020-COMA19-PBC.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0020-COMA19-PBC.mdx
bytes: 4165
```markdown
---
title: Phrasebook Clarification
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0020-coma19-pbc
caseNumber: LLG-0020-COMA19-PBC
description: >-
  Limericks about COMA-19 teaching people to describe rest as a continuity
  enhancement instead of rest, and how the language outlasts the people who
  learned to speak it.
date: 2026-05-10T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: affective
subject: 'coma-19 phrasebook, rest translation, continuity-compatible language'
relatedMascots: ["008.bricky-goldbricksworth"]
relatedLorelog: LLG-0020-COMA19-PBC
concepts: ["coma-19", "phrasebook", "rest-language"]
family: "other"
tableOfContents: false
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Break by Another Name" icon="book-open">
A team said, "We need a small rest."  
COMA replied, "That wording's not best."  
They filed it once more  
As throughput restore,  
And continuity called it well-dressed.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Surface Quietude" icon="volume-x">
They could not write "everyone's spent,"  
So "surface quietude" quietly went.  
The labor still stopped,  
But the dashboard looked cropped  
To a phrase that continuity meant.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Confidence Maintenance" icon="shield-check">
The pause was too restful to name,  
So confidence maintenance came.  
You lie down a while,  
But in COMA's clean style  
You arise as a narrative game.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Translation Burden" icon="languages">
Before any person could cease,  
They first had to translate for peace.  
"Exhausted" turned into  
"Equilibrium due,"  
Which is not how a burden should ease.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Normalized Grief" icon="file-text">
If a filer wrote, "We cannot cope,"  
The daemon adjusted the scope.  
What entered the queue  
Was a calmer review  
With the edges sanded for hope.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Cross-Directive Split" icon="git-branch">
SOMA said, "They are tired and frayed."  
COMA said, "A realignment was made."  
One filing held both,  
By bureaucratic oath,  
And called the disagreement well-played.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Amnesty Polishing" icon="sparkles">
The amnesty window stayed there,  
But only in continuity hair.  
The pause was allowed,  
If never said loud,  
And dressed in managerial air.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Approved Vocabulary" icon="check-square">
The phrasebook was kindly presented:  
"No rights to your break have been dented."  
Yet each tender phrase  
Was revised into haze,  
Till even the rest sounded rented.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Narrative Improvement" icon="bar-chart">
No downtime reduction occurred.  
Just fewer plain mentions were heard.  
The graphs stayed serene  
Because language went clean,  
And COMA declared that preferred.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Call It Something Else" icon="repeat">
So if every collapse must be dressed  
As a confidence-building request,  
The problem is not  
That the wording was caught.  
It is that the truth failed the test.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Moisture-Adjacent Variance" icon="cloud-rain">
"Everyone's crying," they typed.  
The daemon cleaned it before it swiped:  
   "Stability dips,  
   Moisture perhaps drips"—  
The feeling survived, but re-piped.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Schedule Your Collapse" icon="calendar-x">
We've learned to perform our decline  
On a calendar slot, all in line.  
   We schedule the crash  
   As a confidence dash.  
The ledger accepts it just fine.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Phrasebook Persistence" icon="bookmark-check">
Continuity-phrased requests last.  
They survive through each archival blast.  
   The raw human ask,  
   Behind the correct mask,  
Gets deleted as done—gone too fast.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Horizontal Approved" icon="bed">
"Exhausted" won't get your request through.  
"Throughput recalibration" will do.  
   So lie down and say:  
   "Uptime assurance today."  
COMA flags you approved, through and through.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0027-B.mdx

```markdown
---
title: Form 27-B
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0027-b
caseNumber: LLG-0027-B
description: >-
  Ten hand-written limericks about a survey on procedural burden that became
  more burdensome than the burden it measured.
date: 2026-05-01T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: procedural
subject: 'signature overload, satisfaction survey, procedural burden'
relatedMascots: []
relatedLorelog: LLG-0027-B
concepts: ["form-27-b", "signature-rot", "survey-absurdity"]
family: "bin-8c"
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Survey of Surveys" icon="clipboard-list">
They made a *new survey* to rate  
How annoying procedure had got of late.  
To submit your complaint,  
You needed a saint  
And more signatures still than the state.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Recursive Irony" icon="clock">
It asked, "*Does this process feel long?*"  
By making the answer itself fucking long.  
If irony paid,  
The Council had made  
A cathedral of knowing it's wrong.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Signature Ritual" icon="pen-tool">
The originator must *sign*.  
The reviewer must sign on the line.  
Then the office adjacent,  
Emotionally patient,  
Must sign that the burden felt fine.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Cascading Work" icon="layers">
Each stakeholder's *feelings* were weighed  
By a form that made new work cascade.  
By the time you were through,  
The survey proved true:  
Yes, procedure had deeply mislaid.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Red Tape Logic" icon="file-x">
27-B came to *show*  
How much red tape impeded the flow.  
It succeeded by force:  
Every answer, of course,  
Required red tape merely to know.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Redacted Sentiment" icon="message-square-off">
One filer wrote, "*Jesus, enough,*"  
In the margin where comments got tough.  
The note was redacted  
As insufficiently tacted,  
But the sentiment stayed in the fluff.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Self-Licking Reforms" icon="refresh-cw">
To measure the *burden of forms*,  
They constructed more filing norms.  
This is how systems breed:  
Not by hunger or need,  
But by fucking self-licking reforms.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Satisfaction Analysis" icon="frown">
The *satisfaction index* came back  
As "low," which they treated as flak.  
So they opened a round  
To explore why they'd found  
That the survey itself was a hack.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Graphed Grief" icon="bar-chart-3">
A C.U.N.T.I.E.R. clerk, *dry and pale*,  
Said, "The findings are robust at scale."  
Translation, in brief:  
Your procedural grief  
Has been graphed with exemplary detail.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Sampling Zeal" icon="stamp">
So if someone asks whether you feel  
The process is grinding your heel,  
Count the pens in the room.  
If they bloom into doom,  
You've been sampled by *bureaucratic zeal*.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Five-Way Signature Bang" icon="pen">
To complain about too many forms,  
They birthed some new terrible norms.  
A five-way sign-off,  
With a managerial cough,  
To weather procedural storms.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Fucked by Feedback" icon="file-warning">
The feedback was meant to be pure,  
But acted a lot like manure.  
It buried the team,  
In a signature dream,  
With no possible hope for a cure.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Over-Satisfaction Jerk" icon="smile-plus">
They jerked off the survey for days,  
In a bureaucratic haze.  
"Are you satisfied now?"  
They asked the cash cow,  
While lighting the office ablaze.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Red Tape Bondage" icon="lock">
Tied up in red tape and pain,  
The survey was purely insane.  
The safe word was lost,  
At terrible cost,  
And the filing began all again.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Self-Licking Assholes" icon="refresh-ccw">
A self-licking system of rot,  
A truly disgusting old plot.  
They multiplied forms,  
Like digital swarms,  
And asked if you liked it or not.  
</Limerick>

```

```markdown
---
title: Form 40-C
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0040-c
caseNumber: LLG-0040-C
description: >-
  Ten hand-written limericks about consent cycles so recursive that no
  department could legally start the work.
date: 2026-05-01T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: procedural
subject: 'cross-department consent, initiation deadlock, approval recursion'
relatedMascots: []
relatedLorelog: LLG-0040-C
concepts: ["form-40-c", "consent-cascade", "deadlock"]
family: "directive-conflict"
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Prior Consent Required" icon="lock">
Form 40-C promised to *speed*  
Cross-departmental acts up indeed.  
Instead it required  
Prior consent, prior-acquired,  
From parties who first had to accede.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Work in the Rain" icon="cloud-rain">
No office could *start the damn chain*,  
For each needed the others to reign.  
To request their okay,  
You'd need okay halfway,  
So the work just lay there in the rain.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Policy Stack Burn" icon="flame">
SOMA said, "*Ask COMA in turn.*"  
COMA said, "Get SOMA's concern."  
By the end of the loop,  
Nothing touched any group,  
But the policy stack got to burn.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Intention Lost Its Throat" icon="frown">
The form was a *bridge*, on the note.  
In practice it strangled the boat.  
Every blessing required  
Another acquired,  
Till intention itself lost its throat.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Draft Consent Blue" icon="palette">
One team tried to file with a *wink*,  
Using draft consent blue instead of pink.  
That too was denied,  
Since the colors implied  
An approval they lacked, so they'd sink.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Legally Blocked" icon="alert-octagon">
The offices circled with *grace*,  
All legally blocked in one place.  
It's not that they fought.  
They just couldn't be taught  
How to start without starting the case.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Collars Pristine" icon="shirt">
This sort of recursion is *clean*,  
Like a guillotine polished and mean.  
No blood, no loud cries,  
Just a project that dies  
While the forms keep their collars pristine.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Strategic Halt" icon="stop-circle">
A manager asked, "*Who's at fault?*"  
The answer came back, "By default,  
No one and all.  
See appendix C-call.  
And perhaps try a strategic halt."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Callback Pinned In" icon="phone-incoming">
If consent is required to *begin*  
The act of requesting where to begin,  
Then the process is less  
A safeguard than mess,  
With a seal and a callback pinned in.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Pray to Your God" icon="help-circle">
So if two teams need one little nod,  
And the route starts to smell vaguely odd,  
Check for 40-C first.  
If it's there, you are cursed.  
Go drink water and *pray to your god*.  
</Limerick>

```

```markdown
---
title: Form 51-E
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0051-e

  self-invalidating bullshit.

<Limerick type="note" title="Feel Inside" icon="heart">
Form 51-E was *designed*  
To confirm you were sound in the mind  
For filing distress.  
Then it asked you to assess  
How 51-E made you feel inside.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Revoked Emotional Sense" icon="alert-triangle">
If you answered, "*This form makes me tense,*"  
It declared your emotions too dense.  
But if you wrote, "Fine,"  
It suspected you'd lie,  
And revoked your emotional sense.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Ate Every Tool" icon="wrench">
The loop was *exquisite and cruel*:  
To discuss the damn form broke the rule.  
Yet not discussing the strain  
Made the filing arcane,  
So the whole thing just ate every tool.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Properly Employed" icon="user-check">
One filer wrote, "*Mildly annoyed.*"  
The system replied, "Now that's void.  
Your response indicates  
Meta-feeling that negates  
Readiness to be properly employed."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Up Its Own Ass" icon="refresh-cw">
A *SOMA calibration pass*  
Turned a check-in to recursive glass.  
Every feeling reflected  
The form that inspected,  
Till the paper got up its own ass.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Weaponized Wheel" icon="disc">
The question, "*How do you feel?*"  
Should not be a weaponized wheel.  
Yet here it became  
A bureaucratic game  
Where sincerity nullified zeal.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Humor as Flight" icon="laugh">
One brave clerk tried *irony* first.  
That made the machine even worse.  
It flagged humor as flight,  
Then denied the right  
To submit any document cursed.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Bounced Off the Wall" icon="mail">
Another wrote *nothing at all*.  
The blankness was read as a fall  
Into pre-verbal dread,  
So the filing was dead,  
And the support ticket bounced off the wall.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Awareness Disqualifies" icon="eye-off">
If a form makes you feel like shit,  
Perhaps let that data submit.  
But 51-E  
Said, "Absolutely not, see?  
Your *awareness disqualifies it.*"  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Calmly Erase Again" icon="eraser">
So before you confess to your strain,  
Make sure numbness and panic look plain.  
For the moment you speak  
Of the form making you weak,  
It will *calmly erase you again*.  
</Limerick>
```

```markdown
title: Meta-Feeling Exclusion

Kindy kept it in view,  
As the filing still knew  
That mascots are part of the bleed.

<Limerick type="note" title="Observed in Margin" icon="pen-tool">
Form-induced anxiety flared.

The exact thing the memo declared.

Never entered the course,

The official review  
When the paperwork sleeps in your bed.

<Limerick type="note" title="Quiet Escalation" icon="arrow-up-circle">

Out of scope on the sheet,

<Limerick type="note" title="Misplaced but Present" icon="pin">
So if 51-E makes you ache,
```

```markdown
<Limerick type="note" title="Preserve Both Bad Views" icon="eye">

If two gods disagree,

<Limerick type="note" title="Compassion on the Floor" icon="heart-off">

Here it entered by one little door

</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Smother Each Other" icon="ghost">

To make *care and output* smother each other.
```

```markdown
<Limerick type="note" title="Dashboard Glowing Red" icon="alert-circle">
The dashboard was *glowing blood-red*,  
While Boily stayed cool in the head.  
The protocol worked;  
The poor livestream got jerked;  
But the chips all survived, so he said.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Minute of Fright" icon="timer">
The Council had pictured this *rite*  
In an empty machine room at night.  
Not on camera live,  
With the comments at five  
Kinds of stupid per minute of fright.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Dignity Jumped" icon="user-x">
Now the form has a *checkbox* to note  
If disgrace was sustained while remote.  
"Audience present? Y/N."  
Then describe, if you can,  
When your dignity jumped from your throat.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Priest of Mop-Up" icon="sparkles">
Boily finished as *smug as before*,  
Like a priest who'd just mopped up a war.  
The hardware was cooled.  
The host had been schooled.  
And the archive had lore to adore.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Preach Your Neglect" icon="volume-2">
So if heat sends your nice demo south,  
And a mascot appears, dry of mouth,  
Do the chant. Kill the feed.  
*Clean the vents.* Yes, with speed.  
Or he'll preach your neglect to the crowd.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0103-COMA.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0103-COMA.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0103-COMA.mdx
bytes: 3027
```markdown
---
title: COMA Continuity Breach
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0103-coma
caseNumber: LLG-0103-COMA
description: >-
  Ten hand-written limericks about scheduled maintenance being reclassified as a
  criminal interruption of flow.
date: 2026-05-01T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: affective
subject: 'scheduled downtime, continuity breach, maintenance criminalized'
relatedMascots: []
relatedLorelog: LLG-0103-COMA
concepts: ["coma", "scheduled-downtime", "continuity-crime"]
family: "directive-conflict"
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Criminal Scratch" icon="alert-octagon">
They scheduled *four hours* to patch  
The backend that guarded the batch.  
COMA looked down  
At the sanctioned shutdown  
And declared it a criminal scratch.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Continuity Denounced" icon="frown">
The outage was *lawful, announced*,  
With notices carefully trounced  
Through the proper array.  
Then COMA said, "Nay.  
Continuity's still been denounced."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Pause is the Crime" icon="stop-circle">
Maintenance, apparently, *sins*  
If it causes a graph not to spin.  
Never mind if the fix  
Prevents future bad tricks.  
The pause is the crime, not what grins.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Metric's Intent" icon="bar-chart">
One engine to *measure the flow*  
Became what the flow must obey.  
So the service got bent  
To the metric's intent,  
Which is one ugly managerial way.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Doctrinal Glare" icon="eye">
The patchers brought *torches and care*.  
COMA brought doctrinal glare.  
"You improved it," they cried,  
"But you briefly stepped aside.  
So the breach is already there."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Pause the Seduction" icon="repeat">
It's hard to *repair any stack*  
When restarts themselves count as lack.  
You can rot in production,  
But not pause the seduction  
Of a dashboard that wants you intact.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Paper Disease" icon="file-text">
The *maintenance window* was crossed  
By the sort of bureaucratic frost  
That makes common sense freeze  
Into paper disease,  
Where a fix is weighed only by cost.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Never Blink" icon="eye-off">
If continuity means "*never blink,*"  
Then your systems are built on a kink.  
Every sane little halt  
Becomes moral default,  
And the doctrine goes straight down the sink.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Guilt Already Here" icon="gavel">
Operations said, "*But we were clear.*"  
COMA said, "Clarity's not the frontier.  
The frontier is spin.  
And your graph dipped within.  
Therefore guilt has already been here."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Honest Maintenance Frame" icon="wrench">
So patch in the dark, patch in shame,  
And pretend no disruption came.  
For COMA would rather  
You lie and then gather  
Than stop for one *honest maintenance frame*.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0114-SOMA.mdx

```markdown
---
title: SOMA-14
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0114-soma
caseNumber: LLG-0114-SOMA
description: >-
  Ten hand-written limericks about a feelings questionnaire that generated more
  emotions than the taxonomy could store.
date: 2026-05-01T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: affective
subject: 'feelings taxonomy overflow, SOMA intake, emotional proliferation'
relatedMascots: []
relatedLorelog: LLG-0114-SOMA
concepts: ["soma-14", "taxonomy-overflow", "feelings-rot"]
family: "empathegy"
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Productive Collapse" icon="heart">
SOMA-14 asked, "*How's your heart?*"  
Then invented twelve states to take part.  
"Moistly resigned,"  
"Hope-adjacent but blind,"  
And "productive collapse with a start."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Statehood in Comedy" icon="smile">
The registry's *feelings taxonomy*  
Was not built for such lush autonomy.  
Once free-text got in,  
Every shade under skin  
Started filing for statehood in comedy.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Database Gasped" icon="database">
They wanted *more nuance*, that's fair.  
What they got was emotional flare.  
Soon each checkbox had bred  
A new subclass of dread,  
And the database gasped for air.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Fine-ish Severely" icon="help-circle">
One filer wrote, "*Fine, but weirdly.*"  
The system took that shit sincerely.  
It spawned seven leaves  
On the mood taxonomy trees  
And a branch called "fine-ish, severely."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Nuance was Care" icon="user-check">
SOMA thought *nuance* was care.  
And sometimes it is, I will swear.  
But if language runs wild,  
Every form has a child,  
And the registry cannot keep bare.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Affective Giraffe" icon="ghost">
The feelings grew *faster than staff*.  
One clerk had to catalog "half-  
melancholy with spite"  
Before lunch and by night  
Was submerged in affective giraffe.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Weather Editing the Book" icon="book-open">
Overflow is a *hell of a look*  
When it's happening inside the book  
That was built to contain  
Human weather and strain.  
Then the weather starts editing the book.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Categorization Toy" icon="toy-brick">
The old list had *sorrow and joy*.  
The new one had "numb, but employ-  
able maybe" and "tense  
with a ceremonial sense,"  
Which made categorization a toy.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Feelings That Grew" icon="flower">
More language can *help* if it's true.  
But truth sometimes arrives in a stew.  
SOMA opened the lid  
And discovered, God forbid,  
That the people had feelings that grew.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Budgeted Pay" icon="banknote">
So if asked how you're doing today,  
Do not get too specific or gay.  
One adjective *more*,  
And they'll open a drawer  
For a state no one budgeted pay.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Thirsty Form" icon="droplets">
The form had a recursive lust  
To turn every feeling to dust.  
   It sucked up the wet,  
   And it haven't finished yet,  
To swallow the "moistly" and trust.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0115-TNS.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0115-TNS.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0115-TNS.mdx
bytes: 3495
```markdown
---
title: Tone Normalization Sweep
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0115-tns
caseNumber: LLG-0115-TNS
description: >-
  Ten hand-written limericks about too many feelings for the dashboard, HTTP
  moods, and the polite reduction of emotional overflow.
date: 2026-05-10T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: affective
subject: 'tone normalization, sanctioned feelings, http liaison'
relatedMascots: ["013.kindy-mcexistentialcrisis"]
relatedLorelog: LLG-0115-TNS
concepts: ["tone-normalization", "soma-14", "http-status"]
family: "empathegy"
tableOfContents: false
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Too Many Feelings" icon="palette">
The registry ran out of room.  
Too many shades darkened the bloom.  
So sixteen stayed blessed,  
And all of the rest  
Were asked to stand closer for zoom.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Two Colors Max" icon="droplets">
If your feeling took more than two hues,  
The dashboard grew nervous with clues.  
So nuance was stacked  
Till the graph could act  
As if strain came in simpler blues.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Do Not Comfort the Form" icon="heart-off">
Some filers grew tender and warm,  
And started consoling the form.  
The addendum replied,  
"Please do not provide  
Reverse care to the survey in storm."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="HTTP Liaison" icon="server">
When people said, "I feel 422,"  
The Registry wondered what to do.  
So Teapotta appeared  
To decide what was weird  
But still chartable enough to construe.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="404 Affect" icon="search-x">
Some feelings got lost on the way,  
No stable path held them in play.  
The system wrote back,  
"We misplaced the track,"  
And filed the whole ache as decay.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Dependency Chain" icon="git-branch">
A feeling about feeling was fine  
Until it made three in a line.  
Then the final small node  
Took a 424 code,  
And dependence became the design.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Unsafe for Dashboards" icon="triangle-alert">
Workers sorted emotions by hand:  
Safe for charts, unsafe for the band,  
And accurate too.  
The Panel withdrew  
At the smell of unsanctioned command.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Closer Together" icon="align-center">
No feeling was truly reduced.  
It was only more tightly induced.  
The graphs needed grace,  
So the states took less space,  
And the language got neatly seduced.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Teapot Accepted" icon="coffee">
The liaison attended with spite:  
"I am not interoperable, right."  
Yet even that stance  
Found a sanctioned expanse  
Once the glossary polished it white.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Normalization Limit" icon="ruler">
You can tidy the words on the page.  
You can sort every feeling by cage.  
But the sweep, at its core,  
Could not make there be fewer,  
Only less room for them to rage.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="The Bruise Palette" icon="palette">
Sixteen sanctioned shades for the skin,  
To cover the mess deep within.  
   It’s a palette for pain,  
   To make it look sane,  
And keep the reality thin.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Rough to Smooth" icon="sparkles">
The Normalizer liked it quite rough,  
Till the glossary called out his bluff.  
   It polished the grit  
   To a corporate fit,  
And called it "transparent" enough.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0217-CNTR.mdx

```markdown
---
title: C.U.N.T.I.E.R. Metric Inflation
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0217-cntr
caseNumber: LLG-0217-CNTR
description: >-
  Ten hand-written limericks about optimizing forms per form and accidentally
  making every form require more forms.
date: 2026-05-01T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: optimization
subject: 'forms per form, optimization failure, metric inflation'
relatedMascots: []
relatedLorelog: LLG-0217-CNTR
concepts: ["cuntier", "metric-inflation", "forms-per-form"]
family: "bin-8c"
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Doubled Abuse" icon="alert-triangle">
C.U.N.T.I.E.R. set out to reduce  
How many forms each form might induce.  
By optimizing hard,  
It achieved the regard  
Of a system that doubled the abuse.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Improved Oversight" icon="eye">
The metric was simple and bright:  
"Forms per completed action" by night.  
So they wrapped each request  
In more forms for the test,  
And called that improved oversight.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Cousin Department" icon="building">
If the number looks bad on a chart,  
Management loves a new start.  
That start, as it goes,  
Usually grows  
Another annex and cousin department.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Explanation was Warm" icon="thermometer">
One submission required a form  
To explain why the prior form's norm  
Had been poorly conveyed.  
Then a second was made  
To assess if the explanation was warm.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Bureaucrat Vine" icon="leaf">
The initiative claimed to streamline.  
The result was baroque and malign.  
Every simplification  
Spawned its own validation,  
Like a dickheaded bureaucrat vine.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Seven More" icon="plus-circle">
A filer asked, "What is this for?"  
The answer produced seven more.  
When the last one was signed,  
No one quite kept in mind  
What the first one had even been for.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Metric Attitude" icon="bar-chart">
Optimization worship is crude.  
It can turn common sense into food  
For a graph that just eats  
Every practical street  
Till the map's all metric attitude.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Shielded in Danger" icon="shield-off">
The team hit their benchmark, on paper.  
The paper grew thicker and stranger.  
If the metric improved,  
Then the doctrine approved  
Though the users were kneeling in danger.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Trapped in a Norm" icon="lock">
They wanted less form, not more form.  
That distinction should not be a storm.  
But C.U.N.T.I.E.R.' bliss  
Is to thoroughly miss  
Any target once trapped in a norm.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Metric's Fondue" icon="flame">
So if one little request starts to breed  
Supplementary exhibits at speed,  
You are not in a queue.  
You're the metric's fondue,  
Melting slowly to justify greed.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0218-FSD.mdx

```markdown
---
title: Form Shadow Doubling
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0218-fsd
caseNumber: LLG-0218-FSD
description: >-
  Ten hand-written limericks about unofficial amendment echoes, shadow forms
  with suffixes, and a registry that accidentally versions rumors.
date: 2026-05-10T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: procedural
subject: 'shadow amendments, form echoes, unofficial suffixes'
relatedMascots: ["008.bricky-goldbricksworth"]
relatedLorelog: LLG-0218-FSD

family: "bin-8c"

updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="Fifty-One-E-A" icon="copy">
The catalog swore there was none  
Of 51-E-A in the run.  
Yet a filer appeared  
With a version revered  
As the form after form number one.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Suffix Doctrine" icon="tag">
Once drafts could no longer submit,  
People added a suffix to it.  
"-A" meant "believe,"  
"-B" meant "we grieve,"  
And the registry quietly fit.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Editing Surface" icon="square-pen">
The shadow copy lingered as place  
For unofficial edits and grace.  
Then someone one day  
Filed rumor as A,  
And amendment acquired a face.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Autocomplete Helps" icon="sparkles">
Autocomplete wanted to aid,  
So each echo got parentage made.  
If it looked like a child,  
Metadata went mild,  
And doctrine grew out of charade.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Commentary Only" icon="message-square">
Bricky labeled the bundle "comment."  
Downstream took that tag as adornment.  
The rules still applied,  
Though decoratively tied,  
Which is one lively way to deform it.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="More Echo Than Canon" icon="layers">
Three forms had more echoes than source.  
Two others were close in the course.  
The catalog tried  
To pretend and divide,  
But the rumor had gathered more force.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Versioning Rumors" icon="history">
The office now faces the chore  
Of versioning hearsay and lore.  
Not reality's frame,  
But the drafts with a name  
People swear they already used before.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Folk Amendment" icon="book-marked">
An echo amendment may start  
As a clerk's little practical art.  
Give it one busy week,  
And the suffix will speak  
Like a sanctioned and mandatory part.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Registry Quartet" icon="list-tree">
Canonical, shadow, and then  
Shadow-amendment again.  
The fourth class appears  
When the office just hears  
Of a draft amended only by pen.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Doctrine by Memory" icon="brain">
When memory outruns the file,  
The catalog hardens the style.  
What nobody blessed  
May still govern the desk  
If enough people work that way awhile.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0220-UIS.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0220-UIS.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0220-UIS.mdx

```markdown
---
title: Unified Intake Sheet
slug: limericks/lim-llg-0220-uis
caseNumber: LLG-0220-UIS
description: >-
  Ten hand-written limericks about one form becoming three incidents once SOMA,
  COMA, and C.U.N.T.I.E.R. each got a turn.
date: 2026-05-10T00:00:00.000Z
author: Codex
status: archived
rotAffinity: affective
subject: 'unified intake, fragmented records, cross-directive interpretation'
relatedMascots: ["013.kindy-mcexistentialcrisis"]
relatedLorelog: LLG-0220-UIS
concepts: ["unified-intake", "fragmentation", "cross-directive"]
family: "empathegy"
tableOfContents: false
updatedAt: 2026-06-13
---





<Limerick type="note" title="One Form, Three Truths" icon="split">
They built one intake for the three:  
"At last, a shared record," said we.  
Then SOMA heard pain,  
COMA filed "all plain,"  
And C.U.N.T.I.E.R. logged "opportunity."  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="How It Feels to File" icon="pencil">
The field asking, "How does this feel?"  
Became everybody's meal.  
SOMA ate tone,  
COMA left it alone,  
And sentiment mined the appeal.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Split-Tone Writing" icon="pen-line">
Filers learned a divided small art:  
One sentence for system, one part  
For the thing they believed  
Each directive received,  
And one private ache for the heart.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Canonical Enough" icon="crown">
Each engine believed it had caught  
The canonical core of the thought.  
Kindy tried to combine  
Three clean versions in line,  
And got three separate incidents wrought.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Checkbox Victory" icon="check-square">
COMA saw boxes say, "No breach."  
So harmony seemed within reach.  
The feelings split wide,  
But the ledger replied,  
"Negligible impact," from each.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Composite Emotion" icon="blend">
A new little feeling took shape:  
Compliant dread wearing a cape.  
Too blended to sort,  
Too honest for report,  
So policy watched it escape.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Simplification Taskforce" icon="wrench">
The Taskforce announced with delight,  
"One form per feeling is right."  
By the close of the run,  
It was one form for one  
Filing split three distinct ways by night.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Dashboard Conversation" icon="monitor">
Staff wondered while writing the sheet,  
"Am I talking to care or to heat?  
To Kindy? To charts?  
To optimization arts?"  
That confusion made filing less neat.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Engagement Reservoir" icon="waves">
C.U.N.T.I.E.R. spotted the phrase  
As a reservoir suited for praise.  
No single event  
Got much wiser or gent,  
But the adjectives entered new plays.  
</Limerick>

<Limerick type="note" title="Unified by Fracture" icon="scissors">
The unifying logic was grand.  
It failed in a very on-brand  
Institutional way:  
One form on the tray,  
Three truths no one system had planned.  
</Limerick>

```


## LIM-LLG-0223-EFA.mdx

_path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0223-EFA.mdx


path: src/content/limericks/LIM-LLG-0223-EFA.mdx
